Inception
Summary: This document is a System Administration related exercise.
Version: 5.2
Contents
I Preamble 2
II Introduction 3
III General guidelines 4
IV AI Instructions 5
V Mandatory part 7
VI Readme Requirements 12
VII Prerequisites for validation 14
VIII Bonus part 15
IX Submission and peer-evaluation 16
1
Chapter I
Preamble
2
Chapter II
Introduction
This project aims to broaden your knowledge of system administration by using Docker.
You will virtualize several Docker images, creating them in your new personal virtual
machine.
3
Chapter III
General guidelines
ÔÇó This project needs to be done on a Virtual Machine.
ÔÇó All the files required for the configuration of your project must be placed in a srcs
folder.
ÔÇó A Makefile is also required and must be located at the root of your directory. It
must set up your entire application (i.e., it has to build the Docker images using
docker-compose.yml).
ÔÇó This subject requires putting into practice concepts that, depending on your background, you may not have learned yet. Therefore, we advise you not to hesitate to
read a lot of documentation related to Docker usage, as well as anything else you
will find helpful in order to complete this assignment.
4
Chapter IV
AI Instructions
ÔùÅ Context
During your learning journey, AI can assist with many different tasks. Take the time to
explore the various capabilities of AI tools and how they can support your work. However, always approach them with caution and critically assess the results. Whether itÔÇÖs
code, documentation, ideas, or technical explanations, you can never be completely sure
that your question was well-formed or that the generated content is accurate. Your peers
are a valuable resource to help you avoid mistakes and blind spots.
ÔùÅ Main message
Ôÿø Use AI to reduce repetitive or tedious tasks.
Ôÿø Develop prompting skills ÔÇö both coding and non-coding ÔÇö that will benefit your
future career.
Ôÿø Learn how AI systems work to better anticipate and avoid common risks, biases,
and ethical issues.
Ôÿø Continue building both technical and power skills by working with your peers.
Ôÿø Only use AI-generated content that you fully understand and can take responsibility
for.
ÔùÅ Learner rules:
ÔÇó You should take the time to explore AI tools and understand how they work, so
you can use them ethically and reduce potential biases.
ÔÇó You should reflect on your problem before prompting ÔÇö this helps you write clearer,
more detailed, and more relevant prompts using accurate vocabulary.
ÔÇó You should develop the habit of systematically checking, reviewing, questioning,
and testing anything generated by AI.
ÔÇó You should always seek peer review ÔÇö donÔÇÖt rely solely on your own validation.
5
Inception
ÔùÅ Phase outcomes:
ÔÇó Develop both general-purpose and domain-specific prompting skills.
ÔÇó Boost your productivity with effective use of AI tools.
ÔÇó Continue strengthening computational thinking, problem-solving, adaptability, and
collaboration.
ÔùÅ Comments and examples:
ÔÇó YouÔÇÖll regularly encounter situations ÔÇö exams, evaluations, and more ÔÇö where
you must demonstrate real understanding. Be prepared, keep building both your
technical and interpersonal skills.
ÔÇó Explaining your reasoning and debating with peers often reveals gaps in your understanding. Make peer learning a priority.
ÔÇó AI tools often lack your specific context and tend to provide generic responses. Your
peers, who share your environment, can offer more relevant and accurate insights.
ÔÇó Where AI tends to generate the most likely answer, your peers can provide alternative perspectives and valuable nuance. Rely on them as a quality checkpoint.
Ô£ô Good practice:
I ask AI: ÔÇ£How do I test a sorting function?ÔÇØ It gives me a few ideas. I try them out
and review the results with a peer. We refine the approach together.
Ô£ù Bad practice:
I ask AI to write a whole function, copy-paste it into my project. During peerevaluation, I canÔÇÖt explain what it does or why. I lose credibility ÔÇö and I fail my
project.
Ô£ô Good practice:
I use AI to help design a parser. Then I walk through the logic with a peer. We catch
two bugs and rewrite it together ÔÇö better, cleaner, and fully understood.
Ô£ù Bad practice:
I let Copilot generate my code for a key part of my project. It compiles, but I canÔÇÖt
explain how it handles pipes. During the evaluation, I fail to justify and I fail my
project.
6
Chapter V
Mandatory part
This project consists of having you set up a small infrastructure composed of different
services under specific rules. The whole project has to be done in a virtual machine. You
have to use docker compose.
Each Docker image must have the same name as its corresponding service.
Each service has to run in a dedicated container.
For performance reasons, the containers must be built either from the penultimate stable
version of Alpine or Debian. The choice is yours.
You also have to write your own Dockerfiles, one per service. The Dockerfiles must
be called in your docker-compose.yml by your Makefile.
This means you have to build the Docker images of your project yourself. It is then
forbidden to pull ready-made Docker images, as well as using services such as DockerHub
(Alpine/Debian being excluded from this rule).
You then have to set up:
ÔÇó A Docker container that contains NGINX with TLSv1.2 or TLSv1.3 only.
ÔÇó A Docker container that contains WordPress + php-fpm (it must be installed and
configured) only, without nginx.
ÔÇó A Docker container that contains MariaDB only, without nginx.
ÔÇó A volume that contains your WordPress database.
ÔÇó A second volume that contains your WordPress website files.
ÔÇó You must use Docker named volumes for these two persistent storages. Bind
mounts are not allowed for these volumes.
ÔÇó Both named volumes must store their data inside /home/login/data on the host
machine. Replace "login" with your learnerÔÇÖs username.
ÔÇó A docker-network that establishes the connection between your containers.
Your containers have to restart in case of a crash.
7
Inception
A Docker container is not a virtual machine. Thus, it is not
recommended to use any hacky patches based on ÔÇÖtail -fÔÇÖ and similar
methods when trying to run it. Read about how daemons work and
whether itÔÇÖs a good idea to use them or not.
Of course, using network: host or --link or links: is forbidden.
The network line must be present in your docker-compose.yml file.
Your containers must not be started with a command running an
infinite loop. Thus, this also applies to any command used as
entrypoint, or used in entrypoint scripts. The following are a
few prohibited hacky patches: tail -f, bash, sleep infinity, while
true.
Read about PID 1 and the best practices for writing Dockerfiles.
ÔÇó In your WordPress database, there must be two users, one of them being the administrator. The administratorÔÇÖs username canÔÇÖt contain admin/Admin or administrator/Administrator (e.g., admin, administrator, Administrator, admin-123, and
so forth).
Your volumes will be available in the /home/login/data folder of the
host machine using Docker. Of course, you have to replace the login
with yours.
To make things simpler, you have to configure your domain name so it points to your
local IP address.
This domain name must be login.42.fr. Again, you have to use your own login.
For example, if your login is wil, wil.42.fr will redirect to the IP address pointing to
wilÔÇÖs website.
The latest tag is prohibited.
No password must be present in your Dockerfiles.
It is mandatory to use environment variables.
Also, it is mandatory to use a .env file to store environment
variables. It is strongly recommended that you use Docker secrets to
store any confidential information. Any credentials, API keys,
or passwords found in your Git repository (outside of properly
configured secrets) will result in project failure.
Your NGINX container must be the only entrypoint into your
infrastructure via the port 443 only, using the TLSv1.2 or TLSv1.3
protocol.
8
Inception
Here is an example diagram of the expected result:
9
Inception
Below is an example of the expected directory structure:
$> ls -alR
total XX
drwxrwxr-x 3 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 .
drwxrwxrwt 17 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 ..
-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 Makefile
drwxrwxr-x 3 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 secrets
drwxrwxr-x 3 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 srcs
./secrets:
total XX
drwxrwxr-x 2 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 .
drwxrwxr-x 6 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 ..
-rw-r--r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 credentials.txt
-rw-r--r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 db_password.txt
-rw-r--r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 db_root_password.txt
./srcs:
total XX
drwxrwxr-x 3 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 .
drwxrwxr-x 3 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 ..
-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 docker-compose.yml
-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 .env
drwxrwxr-x 5 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 requirements
./srcs/requirements:
total XX
drwxrwxr-x 5 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 .

drwxrwxr-x 4 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 wordpress
./srcs/requirements/mariadb:
total XX

-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 .dockerignore

[...]

drwxrwxr-x 2 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 conf
-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 Dockerfile
-rw-rw-r-- 1 wil wil XXXX avril 42 20:42 .dockerignore
drwxrwxr-x 2 wil wil 4096 avril 42 20:42 tools
[...]
$> cat srcs/.env
DOMAIN_NAME=wil.42.fr
# MYSQL SETUP
MYSQL_USER=XXXXXXXXXXXX
[...]
$>
For obvious security reasons, any credentials, API keys, passwords,
etc., must be saved locally in various ways/files and ignored by git.
Publicly stored credentials will lead you directly to a failure of
the project.
10
Inception
You can store your variables (as a domain name) in an environment
variable file like .env
11
Chapter VI
Readme Requirements
A README.md file must be provided at the root of your Git repository. Its purpose is
to allow anyone unfamiliar with the project (peers, staff, recruiters, etc.) to quickly
understand what the project is about, how to run it, and where to find more information
on the topic.
The README.md must include at least:
ÔÇó The very first line must be italicized and read: This project has been created as part
of the 42 curriculum by <login1>[, <login2>[, <login3>[...]]].
ÔÇó A ÔÇ£DescriptionÔÇØ section that clearly presents the project, including its goal and a
brief overview.
ÔÇó An ÔÇ£InstructionsÔÇØ section containing any relevant information about compilation,
installation, and/or execution.
ÔÇó A ÔÇ£ResourcesÔÇØ section listing classic references related to the topic (documentation, articles, tutorials, etc.), as well as a description of how AI was used ÔÇö
specifying for which tasks and which parts of the project.
Ô×á Additional sections may be required depending on the project (e.g., usage
examples, feature list, technical choices, etc.).
Any required additions will be explicitly listed below.
ÔÇó A Project description section must also explain the use of Docker and the sources
included in the project. It must indicate the main design choices, as well as a
comparison between:
Ôùª Virtual Machines vs Docker
Ôùª Secrets vs Environment Variables
Ôùª Docker Network vs Host Network
Ôùª Docker Volumes vs Bind Mounts
12
Inception
Your README must be written in English.
13
Chapter VII
Prerequisites for validation
In addition to the existing requirements, the following documentation files must be present
at the root of your repository. They must be written in Markdown format (.md).
ÔÇó USER_DOC.md ÔÇö User documentation This file must explain, in clear and simple
terms, how an end user or administrator can:
Ôùª Understand what services are provided by the stack.
Ôùª Start and stop the project.
Ôùª Access the website and the administration panel.
Ôùª Locate and manage credentials.
Ôùª Check that the services are running correctly.
ÔÇó DEV_DOC.md ÔÇö Developer documentation This file must describe how a developer can:
Ôùª Set up the environment from scratch (prerequisites, configuration files, secrets).
Ôùª Build and launch the project using the Makefile and Docker Compose.
Ôùª Use relevant commands to manage the containers and volumes.
Ôùª Identify where the project data is stored and how it persists.
14
Chapter VIII
Bonus part
For this project, the bonus part is intended to be simple.
A Dockerfile must be written for each additional service. Thus, each service will run
inside its own container and will have, if necessary, its dedicated volume.
Bonus list:
ÔÇó Set up redis cache for your WordPress website in order to properly manage the
cache.
ÔÇó Set up a FTP server container pointing to the volume of your WordPress website.
ÔÇó Create a simple static website in the language of your choice except PHP (yes, PHP
is excluded). For example, a showcase site or a site for presenting your resume.
ÔÇó Set up Adminer.
ÔÇó Set up a service of your choice that you think is useful. During the defense, you
will have to justify your choice.
To complete the bonus part, you have the possibility to set up extra
services. In this case, you may open more ports to suit your needs.
The bonus part will only be assessed if the mandatory part is
completed perfectly. Perfect means the mandatory part has been
fully completed and functions without any malfunctions. If you have
not passed ALL the mandatory requirements, your bonus part will not
be evaluated at all.
15
Chapter IX
Submission and peer-evaluation
Submit your assignment in your Git repository as usual. Only the work inside your
repository will be evaluated during the defense. DonÔÇÖt hesitate to double-check the names
of your folders and files to ensure they are correct.
During the evaluation, a brief modification of the project may occasionally be requested. This could involve a minor behaviour change, a few lines of code to write or
rewrite, or an easy-to-add feature.
While this step may not be applicable to every project, you must be prepared for it
if it is mentioned in the evaluation guidelines.
This step is meant to verify your actual understanding of a specific part of the project.
The modification can be performed in any development environment you choose (e.g.,
your usual setup), and it should be feasible within a few minutes ÔÇö unless a specific time
frame is defined as part of the evaluation.
You can, for example, be asked to make a small update to a function or script, modify a
display, or adjust a data structure to store new information, etc.
The details (scope, target, etc.) will be specified in the evaluation guidelines and may
vary from one evaluation to another for the same project.

Chapter VI
Readme Requirements

├ö├ç├│ The very first line must be italicized and read: This project has been created as part
of the 42 curriculum by <login1>[, <login2>[, <login3>[...]]].
├ö├ç├│ A ├ö├ç┬úDescription├ö├ç├ÿ section that clearly presents the project, including its goal and a
brief overview.
├ö├ç├│ An ├ö├ç┬úInstructions├ö├ç├ÿ section containing any relevant information about compilation,
installation, and/or execution.
├ö├ç├│ A ├ö├ç┬úResources├ö├ç├ÿ section listing classic references related to the topic (documentation, articles, tutorials, etc.), as well as a description of how AI was used ├ö├ç├Â
specifying for which tasks and which parts of the project.
├ö├ù├í Additional sections may be required depending on the project (e.g., usage
examples, feature list, technical choices, etc.).
Any required additions will be explicitly listed below.
├ö├ç├│ A Project description section must also explain the use of Docker and the sources
included in the project. It must indicate the main design choices, as well as a
comparison between:
├ö├╣┬¬ Virtual Machines vs Docker
├ö├╣┬¬ Secrets vs Environment Variables
├ö├╣┬¬ Docker Network vs Host Network
├ö├╣┬¬ Docker Volumes vs Bind Mounts
12
Inception
Your README must be written in English.
13
Chapter VII
Prerequisites for validation
In addition to the existing requirements, the following documentation files must be present
at the root of your repository. They must be written in Markdown format (.md).
├ö├ç├│ USER_DOC.md ├ö├ç├Â User documentation This file must explain, in clear and simple
terms, how an end user or administrator can:
├ö├╣┬¬ Understand what services are provided by the stack.
├ö├╣┬¬ Start and stop the project.
├ö├╣┬¬ Access the website and the administration panel.
├ö├╣┬¬ Locate and manage credentials.
├ö├╣┬¬ Check that the services are running correctly.
├ö├ç├│ DEV_DOC.md ├ö├ç├Â Developer documentation This file must describe how a developer can:
├ö├╣┬¬ Set up the environment from scratch (prerequisites, configuration files, secrets).
├ö├╣┬¬ Build and launch the project using the Makefile and Docker Compose.
├ö├╣┬¬ Use relevant commands to manage the containers and volumes.
├ö├╣┬¬ Identify where the project data is stored and how it persists.
14
Chapter VIII
Bonus part
For this project, the bonus part is intended to be simple.
A Dockerfile must be written for each additional service. Thus, each service will run
inside its own container and will have, if necessary, its dedicated volume.
Bonus list:
├ö├ç├│ Set up redis cache for your WordPress website in order to properly manage the
cache.
├ö├ç├│ Set up a FTP server container pointing to the volume of your WordPress website.
├ö├ç├│ Create a simple static website in the language of your choice except PHP (yes, PHP
is excluded). For example, a showcase site or a site for presenting your resume.
├ö├ç├│ Set up Adminer.
├ö├ç├│ Set up a service of your choice that you think is useful. During the defense, you
will have to justify your choice.
To complete the bonus part, you have the possibility to set up extra
services. In this case, you may open more ports to suit your needs.
The bonus part will only be assessed if the mandatory part is
completed perfectly. Perfect means the mandatory part has been
fully completed and functions without any malfunctions. If you have
not passed ALL the mandatory requirements, your bonus part will not
be evaluated at all.
15
Chapter IX
Submission and peer-evaluation
Submit your assignment in your Git repository as usual. Only the work inside your
repository will be evaluated during the defense. Don├ö├ç├ût hesitate to double-check the names
of your folders and files to ensure they are correct.
During the evaluation, a brief modification of the project may occasionally be requested. This could involve a minor behaviour change, a few lines of code to write or
rewrite, or an easy-to-add feature.
While this step may not be applicable to every project, you must be prepared for it
if it is mentioned in the evaluation guidelines.
This step is meant to verify your actual understanding of a specific part of the project.
The modification can be performed in any development environment you choose (e.g.,
your usual setup), and it should be feasible within a few minutes ├ö├ç├Â unless a specific time
frame is defined as part of the evaluation.
You can, for example, be asked to make a small update to a function or script, modify a
display, or adjust a data structure to store new information, etc.
The details (scope, target, etc.) will be specified in the evaluation guidelines and may
vary from one evaluation to another for the same project.
